\hypertarget{class_track_panel}{}\section{Track\+Panel Class Reference}
\label{class_track_panel}\index{Track\+Panel@{Track\+Panel}}


The \hyperlink{class_track_panel}{Track\+Panel} class coordinates updates and operations on the main part of the screen which contains multiple tracks.

\subsection{Detailed Description}
The \hyperlink{class_track_panel}{Track\+Panel} class coordinates updates and operations on the main part of the screen which contains multiple tracks. 

It uses many other classes, but in particular it uses the \hyperlink{class_track_info}{Track\+Info} class to draw the controls area on the left of a track, and the \hyperlink{class_track_artist}{Track\+Artist} class to draw the actual waveforms.

Note that in some of the older code here, e.\+g., \hyperlink{class_track_panel_a484e5dfb5256787bbaf7296b0873a167}{Get\+Label\+Width()}, \char`\"{}\+Label\char`\"{} means the \hyperlink{class_track_info}{Track\+Info} plus the vertical ruler. Confusing relative to \hyperlink{class_label_track}{Label\+Track} labels.

The \hyperlink{class_track_panel}{Track\+Panel} manages multiple tracks and their Track\+Infos.

Note that with stereo tracks there will be one \hyperlink{class_track_info}{Track\+Info} being used by two wavetracks. 

Definition at line 128 of file Track\+Panel.\+h.

This handles adjusting individual samples by hand using the draw tool(s)

There are several member data structure for handling drawing\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item m\+Drawing\+Track\+: keeps track of which track you clicked down on, so drawing doesn\textquotesingle{}t jump to a N\+EW track
\item m\+Drawing\+Track\+Top\+: The top position of the drawing track--makes drawing easier.
\item m\+Drawing\+Start\+Sample\+: The sample you clicked down on, so that you can hold it steady
\item m\+Drawing\+Last\+Drag\+Sample\+: When drag-\/drawing, this keeps track of the last sample you dragged over, so it can smoothly redraw samples that got skipped over
\item m\+Drawing\+Last\+Drag\+Sample\+Value\+: The value of the last 
\end{DoxyItemize}

This method takes care of our different zoom possibilities. It is possible for a user to just \char`\"{}zoom in\char`\"{} or \char`\"{}zoom out,\char`\"{} but it is also possible for a user to drag and select an area that he or she wants to be zoomed in on. We use m\+Zoom\+Start and m\+Zoom\+End to track the beggining and end of such a zoom area. Note that the \hyperlink{class_view_info}{View\+Info} member m\+View\+Info actually keeps track of our zoom constant, so we achieve zooming by altering the zoom constant and forcing a refresh.
